#! ### Build Configuration
#! These combine common choices of building blocks to represent typical builds.

## Everything, all at once.
##
## As fast as possible, tracing, with TUI progress, progress line rendering with autoconfiguration, all transports based on their most mature implementation (HTTP), all `ein` tools, CLI colors and local-time support, JSON output, regex support for rev-specs.
## Can be amended with the `http-client-curl-rustls` feature to avoid `openssl` as backend.
##
## ### Note
##
## When used in conjunction with `http-client-curl-rustls`, the `openssl` crates will still be compiled, but won't be used. To bypass this, disable
## default dependencies and specify the features yourself.
max = ["hashes", "max-control", "fast", "gitoxide-core-tools-query", "gitoxide-core-tools-corpus", "gitoxide-core-blocking-client", "http-client-curl-openssl"]

## Like `max`, but only Rust is allowed.
##
## This is the most compatible build as it won't need a C compiler or C toolchains to build. Thanks to zlib-rs, you don't have to trade off between compatibility and performance.
##
## This uses Rust's HTTP implementation.
##
## As fast as possible, with TUI progress, progress line rendering with auto-configuration, all transports available but less mature pure Rust HTTP implementation, all `ein` tools, CLI colors and local-time support, JSON output, regex support for rev-specs.
max-pure = ["hashes", "max-control", "http-client-reqwest", "gitoxide-core-blocking-client"]

## Like `max`, but with more control for configuration. See the *Package Maintainers* headline for more information.
## Needs to chose its own hash(es).
max-control = ["tracing", "fast", "pretty-cli", "gitoxide-core-tools", "prodash-render-line", "prodash-render-tui", "prodash/render-line-autoconfigure", "gix/revparse-regex"]

## All the good stuff, with less fanciness for smaller binaries.
##
## As fast as possible, progress line rendering, all transports based on their most mature implementation (HTTP), all `ein` tools, CLI colors and local-time support, JSON output.
lean = ["hashes", "fast", "tracing", "pretty-cli", "http-client-curl-openssl", "gitoxide-core-tools-query", "gitoxide-core-tools-corpus", "gitoxide-core-tools", "gitoxide-core-blocking-client", "prodash-render-line"]

## The smallest possible build, best suitable for small single-core machines.
##
## This build is essentially limited to local operations without any fanciness. It does not have `gix clone`.
##
## Optimized for size, no parallelism thus much slower, progress line rendering.
small = ["hashes", "pretty-cli", "prodash-render-line", "is-terminal"]

## Like lean, but uses Rusts async implementations for networking.
##
## This build is more of a demonstration showing how async can work with `gitoxide`, which generally is blocking. This also means that the selection of async transports
## is very limited to only HTTP (without typical `git` configuration) and git over TCP like provided by the `git daemon`.
##
## As fast as possible, progress line rendering, less featureful HTTP (pure Rust) and only `git-daemon` support, all `ein` tools, CLI colors and local-time support, JSON output.
##
## Due to async client-networking not being implemented for most transports, this one supports only the 'git+tcp' and HTTP transport.
## It uses, however, a fully asynchronous networking implementation which can serve a real-world example on how to implement custom async transports.
lean-async = ["hashes", "fast", "tracing", "pretty-cli", "gitoxide-core-tools", "gitoxide-core-tools-query", "gitoxide-core-tools-corpus", "gitoxide-core-async-client", "prodash-render-line"]

#! ### Package Maintainers
#! `*-control` features leave it to you to configure C libraries, involving choices for HTTP transport implementation.
#!
#! Additional features *can* be provided with `--features` and are handled by the [`gix-features` crate](https://docs.rs/gix-features/latest).
#! Note that only one HTTP transport can be enabled at a time. See the *Building Blocks for mutually exclusive networking* headline.

#! ### Building Blocks
#! Typical combinations of features of our dependencies, some of which are referred to in the `gitoxide` crate's code for conditional compilation.

## Provide support for all known hashes. If this isn't enabled, select an individual hash algorithms.
hashes = ["sha1"]
## Enable support for the SHA-1 hash throughout the `gix` crate.
sha1 = ["gix/sha1"]

## Makes the crate execute as fast as possible by supporting parallel computation of otherwise long-running functions.
## If disabled, the binary will be visibly smaller.
fast = ["gix/max-performance", "gix/comfort"]

## Deprecated: identical to `fast`, as the fastest zlib backend is now the pure-Rust zlib-rs.
fast-safe = ["fast"]

## Enable tracing in `gitoxide-core`.
tracing = ["dep:tracing-forest", "dep:tracing-subscriber", "dep:tracing", "gix-features/tracing", "gix-features/tracing-detail"]

## Use `clap` 3.0 to build the prettiest, best documented and most user-friendly CLI at the expense of binary size.
## Provides a terminal user interface for detailed and exhaustive progress.
## Provides a line renderer for leaner progress display, without the need for a full-blown TUI.
pretty-cli = ["gitoxide-core/serde", "prodash/progress-tree", "prodash/progress-tree-log", "prodash/local-time", "env_logger/humantime", "env_logger/color", "env_logger/auto-color"]

## The `--verbose` flag will be powered by an interactive progress mechanism that doubles as log as well as interactive progress
## that appears after a short duration.
prodash-render-line-crossterm = ["prodash-render-line", "prodash/render-line-crossterm", "prodash/signal-hook", "is-terminal", "crosstermion"]

## Progress reporting with a TUI, can then be enabled with the `--progress` flag.
prodash-render-tui = ["prodash/render-tui", "prodash/render-tui-crossterm", "gix/progress-tree", "futures-lite"]

## Progress reporting by visually drawing lines into the terminal without switching to an alternate window.
prodash-render-line = ["prodash/render-line", "prodash-render-line-crossterm", "gix/progress-tree"]

## Prints statistical information to inform about cache efficiency when those are dropped.
## Use this as a way to understand if bigger caches actually produce greater yields.
cache-efficiency-debug = ["gix-features/cache-efficiency-debug"]

##  A way to enable most `gitoxide-core` tools found in `ein tools`, namely `organize` and `estimate hours`.
gitoxide-core-tools = ["gitoxide-core/organize", "gitoxide-core/estimate-hours", "gitoxide-core-tools-archive", "gitoxide-core-tools-clean"]

## A program to perform analytics on a `git` repository, using an auto-maintained sqlite database
gitoxide-core-tools-query = ["gitoxide-core/query"]

## A program to run algorithms on a corpus of repositories, recording each run for later comparison.
gitoxide-core-tools-corpus = ["gitoxide-core/corpus"]

## A sub-command to generate archive from virtual worktree checkouts.
gitoxide-core-tools-archive = ["gitoxide-core/archive"]

## A sub-command to clean the worktree from untracked and ignored files.
gitoxide-core-tools-clean = ["gitoxide-core/clean"]

#! ### Building Blocks for mutually exclusive networking
#! Blocking and async features are mutually exclusive and cause a compile-time error. This also means that `cargo … --all-features` will fail.
#! Within each section, features can be combined.
#!
#! #### Blocking
#! The backends are mutually exclusive, e.g. choose either `curl` or `request`.
#!
## Use blocking client networking.
gitoxide-core-blocking-client = ["gitoxide-core/blocking-client"]
## Support synchronous 'http' and 'https' transports (e.g. for clone, fetch and push) using **curl**.
http-client-curl = ["gix/blocking-http-transport-curl"]
## Implies `http-client-curl` and configures `curl` to use the `rust-tls` backend.
http-client-curl-rustls = ["gix/blocking-http-transport-curl-rustls"]
## Implies `http-client-curl` and configures `curl` to use the `openssl` backend.
http-client-curl-openssl = ["gix/blocking-http-transport-curl-openssl"]
## Support synchronous 'http' and 'https' transports (e.g. for clone, fetch and push) using **reqwest**.
http-client-reqwest = ["gix/blocking-http-transport-reqwest-rust-tls"]

#! #### Async
#!
## Use async client networking.
gitoxide-core-async-client = ["gitoxide-core/async-client", "futures-lite"]

cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/test_merge.rs << 'ENDOFFILE'
// Test reproduction script
use std::io::Write;

fn main() {
    // Simulate the scenario: base has a comment that theirs deletes, and ours has a large insertion before it
    // Build base with 20 lines
    let mut base_lines = Vec::new();
    for i in 0..20 {
        writeln!(&mut base_lines, "line{}", i).unwrap();
    }
    // Add a comment at line 15
    let base_comment_line = 15;
    base_lines.insert(base_comment_line, b"// comment\n".to_vec());
    
    // Build ours: same as base but with 10 new lines inserted before the comment
    let mut ours_lines = Vec::new();
    for i in 0..20 {
        writeln!(&mut ours_lines, "line{}", i).unwrap();
    }
    let ours_insert_at = 15;
    for i in 0..10 {
        writeln!(&mut ours_lines, "new_line{}", i).unwrap();
    }
    ours_lines.push(b"// comment\n".to_vec());
    
    // Build theirs: same as base but comment deleted
    let mut theirs_lines = Vec::new();
    for i in 0..20 {
        writeln!(&mut theirs_lines, "line{}", i).unwrap();
    }
    // Skip the comment
    
    let base: Vec<u8> = base_lines.into_iter().flatten().collect();
    let ours: Vec<u8> = ours_lines.into_iter().flatten().collect();
    let theirs: Vec<u8> = theirs_lines.into_iter().flatten().collect();
    
    // Write to files for inspection
    std::fs::write("/tmp/base.txt", &base).unwrap();
    std::fs::write("/tmp/ours.txt", &ours).unwrap();
    std::fs::write("/tmp/theirs.txt", &theirs).unwrap();
    
    println!("Base: {} bytes, {} lines", base.len(), base.iter().filter(|&&b| b == b'\n').count());
    println!("Ours: {} bytes, {} lines", ours.len(), ours.iter().filter(|&&b| b == b'\n').count());
    println!("Theirs: {} bytes, {} lines", theirs.len(), theirs.iter().filter(|&&b| b == b'\n').count());
    
    // Now compute diff using imara-diff directly
    let input = imara_diff::InternedInput::new(base.as_slice(), ours.as_slice());
    
    println!("\n=== Myers diff base->ours ===");
    let diff = imara_diff::Diff::compute(imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, &input);
    for hunk in diff.hunks() {
        println!("  before: {:?}, after: {:?}", hunk.before, hunk.after);
        // Print the actual lines
        if !hunk.before.is_empty() {
            println!("    BEFORE:");
            for i in hunk.before.clone() {
                let token = input.before[i as usize];
                println!("      [{}] {:?}", i, std::str::from_utf8(&input.interner[token]).unwrap());
            }
        }
        if !hunk.after.is_empty() {
            println!("    AFTER:");
            for i in hunk.after.clone() {
                let token = input.after[i as usize];
                println!("      [{}] {:?}", i, std::str::from_utf8(&input.interner[token]).unwrap());
            }
        }
    }
    
    println!("\n=== Histogram diff base->ours ===");
    let diff = imara_diff::Diff::compute(imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram, &input);
    for hunk in diff.hunks() {
        println!("  before: {:?}, after: {:?}", hunk.before, hunk.after);
        if !hunk.before.is_empty() {
            println!("    BEFORE:");
            for i in hunk.before.clone() {
                let token = input.before[i as usize];
                println!("      [{}] {:?}", i, std::str::from_utf8(&input.interner[token]).unwrap());
            }
        }
        if !hunk.after.is_empty() {
            println!("    AFTER:");
            for i in hunk.after.clone() {
                let token = input.after[i as usize];
                println!("      [{}] {:?}", i, std::str::from_utf8(&input.interner[token]).unwrap());
            }
        }
    }
    
    // Now the merge
    println!("\n=== Merge with Myers ===");
    let mut out = Vec::new();
    let mut merge_input = imara_diff::InternedInput::default();
    let options = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Options {
        diff_algorithm: imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers,
        conflict: gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Conflict::Keep {
            style: gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::ConflictStyle::Merge,
            marker_size: std::num::NonZeroU8::new(7).unwrap(),
        },
    };
    let labels = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Labels::default();
    let resolution = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::function::merge(
        &mut out, &mut merge_input, labels, &ours, &base, &theirs, options,
    );
    println!("Resolution: {:?}", resolution);
    println!("Output:\n{}", String::from_utf8_lossy(&out));
    
    println!("\n=== Merge with Histogram ===");
    out.clear();
    merge_input.clear();
    let options = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Options {
        diff_algorithm: imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram,
        conflict: gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Conflict::Keep {
            style: gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::ConflictStyle::Merge,
            marker_size: std::num::NonZeroU8::new(7).unwrap(),
        },
    };
    let resolution = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::function::merge(
        &mut out, &mut merge_input, labels, &ours, &base, &theirs, options,
    );
    println!("Resolution: {:?}", resolution);
    println!("Output:\n{}", String::from_utf8_lossy(&out));
}
ENDOFFILE
echo "done"

# Quick script to understand diff behavior
base = []
for i in range(20):
    base.append(f"line{i}")
# Add comment at position 15
base.insert(15, "// comment")
# base now has 21 lines

ours = []
for i in range(20):
    ours.append(f"line{i}")
# Insert 10 new lines before the comment (at position 15)
for i in range(10):
    ours.append(f"new_line{i}")
ours.append("// comment")
# ours now has 31 lines

theirs = []
for i in range(20):
    theirs.append(f"line{i}")
# Skip comment - theirs has 20 lines

print("Base:", base)
print()
print("Ours:", ours)
print()
print("Theirs:", theirs)
EOF

fn main() {
    use std::io::Write;

    // Better test case matching the PR description:
    // base: lines 0-14, then comment, then lines 15-19
    // ours: lines 0-14, then 10 new lines, then comment, then lines 15-19
    // theirs: lines 0-14, then lines 15-19 (no comment)
    
    let mut base = Vec::new();
    for i in 0..15 {
        writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap();
    }
    writeln!(&mut base, "// comment").unwrap();
    for i in 15..20 {
        writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap();
    }
    
    let mut ours = Vec::new();
    for i in 0..15 {
        writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap();
    }
    for i in 0..10 {
        writeln!(&mut ours, "new_line{}", i).unwrap();
    }
    writeln!(&mut ours, "// comment").unwrap();
    for i in 15..20 {
        writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap();
    }
    
    let mut theirs = Vec::new();
    for i in 0..15 {
        writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap();
    }
    // no comment
    for i in 15..20 {
        writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap();
    }
    
    println!("Base: {} bytes", base.len());
    println!("Ours: {} bytes", ours.len());
    println!("Theirs: {} bytes", theirs.len());
    
    // Compute diffs directly
    let input_base_ours = imara_diff::InternedInput::new(base.as_slice(), ours.as_slice());
    let input_base_theirs = imara_diff::InternedInput::new(base.as_slice(), theirs.as_slice());
    
    println!("\n=== Myers diff base->ours ===");
    let diff = imara_diff::Diff::compute(imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, &input_base_ours);
    for hunk in diff.hunks() {
        println!("  before: {:?}, after: {:?}", hunk.before, hunk.after);
        if !hunk.before.is_empty() {
            print!("    BEFORE lines: ");
            for i in hunk.before.clone() {
                print!("{} ", i);
            }
            println!();
        }
        if !hunk.after.is_empty() {
            print!("    AFTER lines: ");
            for i in hunk.after.clone() {
                print!("{} ", i);
            }
            println!();
        }
    }
    
    println!("\n=== Myers diff base->theirs ===");
    let diff = imara_diff::Diff::compute(imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, &input_base_theirs);
    for hunk in diff.hunks() {
        println!("  before: {:?}, after: {:?}", hunk.before, hunk.after);
        if !hunk.before.is_empty() {
            print!("    BEFORE lines: ");
            for i in hunk.before.clone() {
                print!("{} ", i);
            }
            println!();
        }
        if !hunk.after.is_empty() {
            print!("    AFTER lines: ");
            for i in hunk.after.clone() {
                print!("{} ", i);
            }
            println!();
        }
    }
    
    println!("\n=== Histogram diff base->ours ===");
    let diff = imara_diff::Diff::compute(imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram, &input_base_ours);
    for hunk in diff.hunks() {
        println!("  before: {:?}, after: {:?}", hunk.before, hunk.after);
        if !hunk.before.is_empty() {
            print!("    BEFORE lines: ");
            for i in hunk.before.clone() {
                print!("{} ", i);
            }
            println!();
        }
        if !hunk.after.is_empty() {
            print!("    AFTER lines: ");
            for i in hunk.after.clone() {
                print!("{} ", i);
            }
            println!();
        }
    }
    
    println!("\n=== Histogram diff base->theirs ===");
    let diff = imara_diff::Diff::compute(imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram, &input_base_theirs);
    for hunk in diff.hunks() {
        println!("  before: {:?}, after: {:?}", hunk.before, hunk.after);
        if !hunk.before.is_empty() {
            print!("    BEFORE lines: ");
            for i in hunk.before.clone() {
                print!("{} ", i);
            }
            println!();
        }
        if !hunk.after.is_empty() {
            print!("    AFTER lines: ");
            for i in hunk.after.clone() {
                print!("{} ", i);
            }
            println!();
        }
    }
    
    // Now the merge
    println!("\n=== Merge with Myers ===");
    let mut out = Vec::new();
    let mut merge_input = imara_diff::InternedInput::default();
    let options = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Options {
        diff_algorithm: imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers,
        conflict: gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Conflict::Keep {
            style: gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::ConflictStyle::Merge,
            marker_size: std::num::NonZeroU8::new(7).unwrap(),
        },
    };
    let labels = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Labels::default();
    let resolution = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::function::merge(
        &mut out, &mut merge_input, labels, &ours, &base, &theirs, options,
    );
    println!("Resolution: {:?}", resolution);
    if resolution == gix_merge::blob::Resolution::Conflict {
        println!("Output:\n{}", String::from_utf8_lossy(&out));
    }
    
    println!("\n=== Merge with Histogram ===");
    out.clear();
    merge_input.clear();
    let options = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Options {
        diff_algorithm: imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram,
        conflict: gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Conflict::Keep {
            style: gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::ConflictStyle::Merge,
            marker_size: std::num::NonZeroU8::new(7).unwrap(),
        },
    };
    let resolution = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::function::merge(
        &mut out, &mut merge_input, labels, &ours, &base, &theirs, options,
    );
    println!("Resolution: {:?}", resolution);
    if resolution == gix_merge::blob::Resolution::Conflict {
        println!("Output:\n{}", String::from_utf8_lossy(&out));
    }
}
ENDOFFILE

Let me focus on the core issue. Let me look at the `take_intersecting` function more carefully. The issue is about how overlap detection works.

Let me re-read the merge algorithm:

1. Compute diff base→current (ours). This gives hunks with `side = Side::Current`.
2. Compute diff base→other (theirs). This gives hunks with `side = Side::Other`.
3. Sort all hunks by `before.start`.
4. Iterate through sorted hunks, using `take_intersecting` to find overlapping hunks.

The `take_intersecting` function:
1. Takes the next hunk from iterator into `input`.
2. Collects all following hunks from the *other* side that overlap with `input` into `intersecting`.
3. Then also collects following hunks from the *same* side that overlap with `intersecting`.

The overlap detection (`left_overlaps_right`) checks if `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` or `(right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start)`.

Now, what happens when we have:
- Ours hunk: an insertion (before=empty, after=some range)
- Theirs hunk: a deletion (before=some range, after=empty)

If the insertion hunk from ours is before=[15, 15), after=[15, 25) (insert 10 lines at position 15), and the deletion hunk from theirs is before=[15, 16), after=[15, 15) (delete 1 line at position 15)...

Wait, let me reconsider. The base has the comment at line 15 (0-indexed). 

For base→ours: 10 new lines are inserted before the comment. The diff might show:
- Hunk 1: before=[15, 15), after=[15, 25) — insertion of 10 lines at line 15

Actually, wait. If we insert lines before the comment, the comment is now at a different position but unchanged. The diff should just show an insertion with before=empty. 

For base→theirs: the comment at line 15 is deleted:
- Hunk 1: before=[15, 16), after=[15, 15) — deletion of 1 line at line 15

These two hunks should NOT overlap because the ours hunk has empty before range which should not overlap with anything.

But wait, the issue might be more subtle. What if the Myers diff for base→ours produces a different hunk? Let me check: what does Myers produce for "insert 10 lines before an existing line"?

Actually, let me look at the problem from a different angle. The PR says the conflict region spans lines 78-105 of the merged output. This is a large region. The false conflict includes the comment AND several lines of code above it.

Let me think about what could cause this...

The key insight from the PR is: "gix sees the comment deletion as conflicting with the large insertion above it."

So the Myers diff for base→ours must be producing a hunk that includes the comment as part of a "change" rather than a separate insertion. For example, instead of:
- Hunk: before=[], after=[32, 102) (pure insertion of 70 lines)

It might produce:
- Hunk: before=[32, 33), after=[32, 103) (replace 1 line with 71 lines)

If the Myers algorithm sees that the comment at position 32 in base matches the comment at position 102 in ours, it might group the insertion + the matching line as a single "modify" hunk. This would cause the before range [32, 33) to overlap with the deletion hunk from theirs (which has before=[32, 33)).

     1	// Modified for gitoxide from the upstream imara-diff crate.
     2	// Upstream source: git cat-file -p 32d1e45d3df061e6ccba6db7fdce92db29e345d8:src/myers.rs
     3	
     4	use std::ptr::NonNull;
     5	
     6	use crate::intern::Token;
     7	use crate::myers::middle_snake::{MiddleSnakeSearch, SearchResult};
     8	use crate::myers::slice::FileSlice;
     9	use crate::util::sqrt;
    10	
    11	mod middle_snake;
    12	mod preprocess;
    13	mod slice;
    14	
    15	/// Computes a diff using the Myers algorithm.
    16	///
    17	/// # Parameters
    18	///
    19	/// * `before` - The token sequence from the first file
    20	/// * `after` - The token sequence from the second file
    21	/// * `removed` - Output array marking removed tokens
    22	/// * `added` - Output array marking added tokens
    23	/// * `minimal` - If true, disables heuristics to guarantee a minimal diff
    24	pub fn diff(before: &[Token], after: &[Token], removed: &mut [bool], added: &mut [bool], minimal: bool) {
    25	    // Preprocess the files by removing parts of the file that are not contained in the other file at all.
    26	    // This process remaps the token indices so we have to account for that during the rest of the diff
    27	    let (before, after) = preprocess::preprocess(before, after, removed, added);
    28	
    29	    // Perform the actual diff
    30	    Myers::new(before.tokens.len(), after.tokens.len()).run(
    31	        FileSlice::new(&before, removed),
    32	        FileSlice::new(&after, added),
    33	        minimal,
    34	    );
    35	}
    36	
    37	/// Minimum edit cost before heuristics are applied to avoid quadratic behavior.
    38	const HEUR_MIN_COST: u32 = 256;
    39	/// Minimum value for the maximum cost threshold.
    40	const MAX_COST_MIN: u32 = 256;
    41	
    42	/// The Myers diff algorithm implementation with linear space complexity.
    43	///
    44	/// This structure maintains the internal state needed to compute diffs using
    45	/// Myers' algorithm with forward and backward search.
    46	pub struct Myers {
    47	    /// The backing memory for k-vectors.
    48	    kvec: NonNull<[i32]>,
    49	    /// Pointer to the forward search k-vector.
    50	    kforward: NonNull<i32>,
    51	    /// Pointer to the backward search k-vector.
    52	    kbackward: NonNull<i32>,
    53	    /// Maximum edit cost before applying heuristics.
    54	    max_cost: u32,
    55	}
    56	
    57	impl Drop for Myers {
    58	    fn drop(&mut self) {
    59	        unsafe { drop(Box::from_raw(self.kvec.as_ptr())) }
    60	    }
    61	}
    62	
    63	impl Myers {
    64	    fn new(len1: usize, len2: usize) -> Self {
    65	        let ndiags = len1 + len2 + 3;
    66	        let kvec: *mut [i32] = Box::into_raw(vec![0; 2 * ndiags + 2].into_boxed_slice());
    67	        let (kforward, kbackward) = unsafe {
    68	            (
    69	                NonNull::new_unchecked((kvec as *mut i32).add(len2 + 1)),
    70	                NonNull::new_unchecked((kvec as *mut i32).add(ndiags + len2 + 1)),
    71	            )
    72	        };
    73	        Self {
    74	            kvec: unsafe { NonNull::new_unchecked(kvec) },
    75	            kforward,
    76	            kbackward,
    77	            max_cost: sqrt(ndiags).max(MAX_COST_MIN),
    78	        }
    79	    }
    80	
    81	    fn run<'f>(&mut self, mut file1: FileSlice<'f>, mut file2: FileSlice<'f>, mut need_min: bool) {
    82	        loop {
    83	            file1.strip_common(&mut file2);
    84	
    85	            if file1.is_empty() {
    86	                file2.mark_changed();
    87	                return;
    88	            } else if file2.is_empty() {
    89	                file1.mark_changed();
    90	                return;
    91	            }
    92	
    93	            let split = self.split(&file1, &file2, need_min);
    94	            self.run(
    95	                file1.borrow().slice(..split.token_idx1 as u32),
    96	                file2.borrow().slice(..split.token_idx2 as u32),
    97	                split.minimized_lo,
    98	            );
    99	
   100	            file1 = file1.slice(split.token_idx1 as u32..);
   101	            file2 = file2.slice(split.token_idx2 as u32..);
   102	            need_min = split.minimized_hi
   103	        }
   104	    }
   105	
   106	    /// See "An O(ND) Difference Algorithm and its Variations", by Eugene Myers.
   107	    /// Basically considers a "box" (off1, off2, lim1, lim2) and scan from both
   108	    /// the forward diagonal starting from (off1, off2) and the backward diagonal
   109	    /// starting from (lim1, lim2). If the K values on the same diagonal crosses
   110	    /// returns the furthest point of reach. We might encounter expensive edge cases
   111	    /// using this algorithm, so a little bit of heuristic is needed to cut the
   112	    /// search and to return a suboptimal point.
   113	    fn split(&mut self, file1: &FileSlice, file2: &FileSlice, need_min: bool) -> Split {
   114	        let mut forward_search = unsafe { MiddleSnakeSearch::<false>::new(self.kforward, file1, file2) };
   115	        let mut backwards_search = unsafe { MiddleSnakeSearch::<true>::new(self.kbackward, file1, file2) };
   116	        let is_odd = file2.len().wrapping_sub(file1.len()) & 1 != 0;
   117	
   118	        let mut ec = 0;
   119	
   120	        while ec <= self.max_cost {
   121	            let mut found_snake = false;
   122	            forward_search.next_d();
   123	            if is_odd {
   124	                if let Some(res) = forward_search.run(file1, file2, |k, token_idx1| {
   125	                    backwards_search.contains(k) && backwards_search.x_pos_at_diagonal(k) <= token_idx1
   126	                }) {
   127	                    #[cfg(test)]
   128	                    cov_mark::hit!(ODD_SPLIT);
   129	                    match res {
   130	                        SearchResult::Snake => found_snake = true,
   131	                        SearchResult::Found { token_idx1, token_idx2 } => {
   132	                            return Split {
   133	                                token_idx1,
   134	                                token_idx2,
   135	                                minimized_lo: true,
   136	                                minimized_hi: true,
   137	                            };
   138	                        }
   139	                    }
   140	                }
   141	            } else {
   142	                found_snake |= forward_search.run(file1, file2, |_, _| false).is_some()
   143	            };
   144	
   145	            backwards_search.next_d();
   146	            if !is_odd {
   147	                if let Some(res) = backwards_search.run(file1, file2, |k, token_idx1| {
   148	                    forward_search.contains(k) && token_idx1 <= forward_search.x_pos_at_diagonal(k)
   149	                }) {
   150	                    #[cfg(test)]
   151	                    cov_mark::hit!(EVEN_SPLIT);
   152	                    match res {
   153	                        SearchResult::Snake => found_snake = true,
   154	                        SearchResult::Found { token_idx1, token_idx2 } => {
   155	                            return Split {
   156	                                token_idx1,
   157	                                token_idx2,
   158	                                minimized_lo: true,
   159	                                minimized_hi: true,
   160	                            };
   161	                        }
   162	                    }
   163	                }
   164	            } else {
   165	                found_snake |= backwards_search.run(file1, file2, |_, _| false).is_some()
   166	            };
   167	
   168	            if need_min {
   169	                ec += 1;
   170	                continue;
   171	            }
   172	
   173	            // If the edit cost is above the heuristic trigger and if
   174	            // we got a good snake, we sample current diagonals to see
   175	            // if some of them have reached an "interesting" path. Our
   176	            // measure is a function of the distance from the diagonal
   177	            // corner (i1 + i2) penalized with the distance from the
   178	            // mid-diagonal itself. If this value is above the current
   179	            // edit cost times a magic factor (XDL_K_HEUR) we consider
   180	            // it interesting.
   181	            if found_snake && ec > HEUR_MIN_COST {
   182	                if let Some((token_idx1, token_idx2)) = forward_search.found_snake(ec, file1, file2) {
   183	                    return Split {
   184	                        token_idx1,
   185	                        token_idx2,
   186	                        minimized_lo: true,
   187	                        minimized_hi: false,
   188	                    };
   189	                }
   190	
   191	                if let Some((token_idx1, token_idx2)) = backwards_search.found_snake(ec, file1, file2) {
   192	                    return Split {
   193	                        token_idx1,
   194	                        token_idx2,
   195	                        minimized_lo: false,
   196	                        minimized_hi: true,
   197	                    };
   198	                }
   199	            }
   200	
   201	            ec += 1;
   202	        }
   203	
   204	        let (distance_forward, token_idx1_forward) = forward_search.best_position(file1, file2);
   205	        let (distance_backwards, token_idx1_backwards) = backwards_search.best_position(file1, file2);
   206	        if distance_forward > file1.len() as isize + file2.len() as isize - distance_backwards {
   207	            Split {
   208	                token_idx1: token_idx1_forward,
   209	                token_idx2: (distance_forward - token_idx1_forward as isize) as i32,
   210	                minimized_lo: true,
   211	                minimized_hi: false,
   212	            }
   213	        } else {
   214	            Split {
   215	                token_idx1: token_idx1_backwards,
   216	                token_idx2: (distance_backwards - token_idx1_backwards as isize) as i32,
   217	                minimized_lo: false,
   218	                minimized_hi: true,
   219	            }
   220	        }
   221	    }
   222	}
   223	
   224	/// Represents a split point in the divide-and-conquer approach.
   225	///
   226	/// The split divides the problem into two subproblems at the given token positions.
   227	#[derive(Debug)]
   228	struct Split {
   229	    /// Token index in the first sequence where the split occurs.
   230	    token_idx1: i32,
   231	    /// Token index in the second sequence where the split occurs.
   232	    token_idx2: i32,
   233	    /// Whether the lower subproblem was minimized.
   234	    minimized_lo: bool,
   235	    /// Whether the upper subproblem was minimized.
   236	    minimized_hi: bool,
   237	}
   238	
   239	// /// the mapping performed during preprocessing makes it impossible to directly call
   240	// /// the `sink` during the diff itself. Instead, `file.changed` is set to true for all
   241	// /// tokens that are changed

     2	// Upstream source: git cat-file -p 32d1e45d3df061e6ccba6db7fdce92db29e345d8:src/myers/preprocess.rs

     4	use crate::intern::Token;
     5	use crate::myers::sqrt;
     6	
     7	/// Preprocesses token sequences by removing tokens that don't appear in the other sequence.
     8	///
     9	/// This optimization reduces the problem size for the Myers algorithm, improving performance
    10	/// for files with many unique tokens.
    11	pub fn preprocess<'a>(
    12	    before: &[Token],
    13	    after: &[Token],
    14	    removed: &'a mut [bool],
    15	    added: &'a mut [bool],
    16	) -> (PreprocessedFile, PreprocessedFile) {
    17	    let (occurrences_before, occurrences_after) = token_occurrences(before, after);
    18	    let file1 = PreprocessedFile::new(&occurrences_before, before, removed);
    19	    let file2 = PreprocessedFile::new(&occurrences_after, after, added);
    20	    (file1, file2)
    21	}
    22	
    23	fn token_occurrences(file1: &[Token], file2: &[Token]) -> (Vec<Occurrences>, Vec<Occurrences>) {
    24	    const MAX_EQLIMIT: u32 = 1024;
    25	
    26	    // compute the limit after which tokens are treated as `Occurrences::COMMON`
    27	    let eqlimit1 = sqrt(file1.len()).min(MAX_EQLIMIT);
    28	    let eqlimit2 = sqrt(file2.len()).min(MAX_EQLIMIT);
    29	
    30	    // first collect how often each token occurs in a file
    31	    let mut occurrences1 = Vec::new();
    32	    for token in file1 {
    33	        let bucket = token.0 as usize;
    34	        if bucket >= occurrences1.len() {
    35	            occurrences1.resize(bucket + 1, 0u32);
    36	        }
    37	        occurrences1[bucket] += 1;
    38	    }
    39	
    40	    // do the same thing for
    41	    let mut occurrences2 = Vec::new();
    42	    let token_occurrences2: Vec<_> = file2
    43	        .iter()
    44	        .map(|token| {
    45	            let bucket = token.0 as usize;
    46	            if bucket >= occurrences2.len() {
    47	                occurrences2.resize(bucket + 1, 0);
    48	            }
    49	            occurrences2[bucket] += 1;
    50	            let occurrences1 = *occurrences1.get(bucket).unwrap_or(&0);
    51	            Occurrences::from_occurrences(occurrences1, eqlimit2)
    52	        })
    53	        .collect();
    54	
    55	    let token_occurrences1: Vec<_> = file1
    56	        .iter()
    57	        .map(|token| {
    58	            let bucket = token.0 as usize;
    59	            let occurrences2 = *occurrences2.get(bucket).unwrap_or(&0);
    60	            Occurrences::from_occurrences(occurrences2, eqlimit1)
    61	        })
    62	        .collect();
    63	
    64	    (token_occurrences1, token_occurrences2)
    65	}
    66	
    67	/// Categorizes how frequently a token appears in a file.
    68	#[derive(Clone, Copy, Debug)]
    69	enum Occurrences {
    70	    /// Token does not occur in the other file.
    71	    None,
    72	    /// Token occurs at least once in the other file.
    73	    Some,
    74	    /// Token occurs very frequently in the other file (exact threshold depends on file size).
    75	    /// Such tokens are usually empty lines or braces and are often not meaningful to a diff.
    76	    Common,
    77	}
    78	
    79	impl Occurrences {
    80	    pub fn from_occurrences(occurrences: u32, eqlimit: u32) -> Occurrences {
    81	        if occurrences == 0 {
    82	            Occurrences::None
    83	        } else if occurrences >= eqlimit {
    84	            Occurrences::Common
    85	        } else {
    86	            Occurrences::Some
    87	        }
    88	    }
    89	}
    90	
    91	/// A file after preprocessing has removed unmatched tokens.
    92	#[derive(Debug)]
    93	pub struct PreprocessedFile {
    94	    /// Maps from new token positions to original positions in the unpreprocessed file.
    95	    pub indices: Vec<u32>,
    96	    /// The tokens that remain after preprocessing.
    97	    pub tokens: Vec<Token>,
    98	}
    99	
   100	impl PreprocessedFile {
   101	    fn new(token_occurrences: &[Occurrences], tokens: &[Token], changed: &mut [bool]) -> PreprocessedFile {
   102	        let (tokens, indices) = prune_unmatched_tokens(tokens, token_occurrences, changed);
   103	        PreprocessedFile { indices, tokens }
   104	    }
   105	}
   106	
   107	fn prune_unmatched_tokens(
   108	    file: &[Token],
   109	    token_status: &[Occurrences],
   110	    changed: &mut [bool],
   111	) -> (Vec<Token>, Vec<u32>) {
   112	    assert_eq!(token_status.len(), file.len());
   113	    file.iter()
   114	        .zip(token_status)
   115	        .enumerate()
   116	        .filter_map(|(i, (&token, &status))| {
   117	            let prune = match status {
   118	                Occurrences::None => true,
   119	                Occurrences::Some => false,
   120	                Occurrences::Common => should_prune_common_line(token_status, i),
   121	            };
   122	            if prune {
   123	                changed[i] = true;
   124	                None
   125	            } else {
   126	                Some((token, i as u32))
   127	            }
   128	        })
   129	        .unzip()
   130	}
   131	
   132	// TODO do not unnecessarily rescan lines
   133	fn should_prune_common_line(token_status: &[Occurrences], pos: usize) -> bool {
   134	    const WINDOW_SIZE: usize = 100;
   135	
   136	    let mut unmatched_before = 0;
   137	    let mut common_before = 0;
   138	
   139	    let start = pos.saturating_sub(WINDOW_SIZE);
   140	    for status in token_status[start..pos].iter().rev() {
   141	        match status {
   142	            Occurrences::None => {
   143	                unmatched_before += 1;
   144	            }
   145	            Occurrences::Common => {
   146	                common_before += 1;
   147	            }
   148	            Occurrences::Some => break,
   149	        }
   150	    }
   151	
   152	    if unmatched_before == 0 {
   153	        return false;
   154	    }
   155	
   156	    let end = token_status.len().min(pos + WINDOW_SIZE);
   157	    let mut unmatched_after = 0;
   158	    let mut common_after = 0;
   159	    for status in token_status[pos..end].iter() {
   160	        match status {
   161	            Occurrences::None => {
   162	                unmatched_after += 1;
   163	            }
   164	            Occurrences::Common => {
   165	                common_after += 1;
   166	            }
   167	            Occurrences::Some => break,
   168	        }
   169	    }
   170	
   171	    if unmatched_after == 0 {
   172	        return false;
   173	    }
   174	
   175	    let common = common_before + common_after;
   176	    let unmatched = unmatched_before + unmatched_after;
   177	
   178	    unmatched > 3 * common
   179	}
   180	
   181	#[cfg(test)]
   182	mod tests {
   183	    use super::{should_prune_common_line, Occurrences};

   185	    #[test]
   186	    fn common_line_pruning_ignores_distant_context() {
   187	        let mut token_status = vec![Occurrences::Some; 700];
   188	        token_status[100..400].fill(Occurrences::None);
   189	        token_status[400..450].fill(Occurrences::None);
   190	        token_status[450..500].fill(Occurrences::Common);
   191	        token_status[500..550].fill(Occurrences::Common);
   192	        token_status[550..600].fill(Occurrences::None);
   193	
   194	        assert!(
   195	            !should_prune_common_line(&token_status, 500),
   196	            "only the last 100 items before the current line should contribute to the backward scan"
   197	        );
   198	    }

cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/repro_test.rs << 'ENDOFFILE'
// Simulate the exact scenario from the PR description but simplified
// We need: base with a line, ours inserts many lines before that line, theirs deletes that line

fn run_test(description: &str, base: &[u8], ours: &[u8], theirs: &[u8]) {
    let mut output = Vec::new();
    let mut input = imara_diff::InternedInput::new(&[][..], &[][..]);
    
    for algo in [imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram] {
        let options = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Options {
            diff_algorithm: algo,
            conflict: gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Conflict::Keep {
                style: gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::ConflictStyle::Merge,
                marker_size: std::num::NonZeroU8::new(7).unwrap(),
            },
        };
        let labels = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Labels::default();
        
        output.clear();
        input.clear();
        
        let resolution = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::function::merge(
            &mut output, &mut input, labels, ours, base, theirs, options,
        );
        println!("{} [{}]: {:?}", description, 
            if algo == imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers { "Myers" } else { "Histogram" },
            resolution);
        if resolution == gix_merge::blob::Resolution::Conflict {
            println!("  Output:\n{}", String::from_utf8_lossy(&output));
        }
    }
}

fn main() {
    use std::io::Write;
    
    // Test 1: Simple case - insert lines before a unique line, then delete that unique line
    println!("=== Test 1: Insert before unique line, delete that line ===");
    {
        let base = b"line_a\nunique_comment\nline_b\n";
        let ours = b"line_a\nnew1\nnew2\nnew3\nunique_comment\nline_b\n";
        let theirs = b"line_a\nline_b\n";
        run_test("Test1", base, ours, theirs);
    }
    
    // Test 2: More lines around the comment
    println!("\n=== Test 2: More context lines ===");
    {
        let mut base = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..10 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut base, "// unique comment").unwrap();
        for i in 10..20 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut ours = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..10 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        for i in 0..10 { writeln!(&mut ours, "new_line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut ours, "// unique comment").unwrap();
        for i in 10..20 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut theirs = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..10 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        for i in 10..20 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        run_test("Test2", &base, &ours, &theirs);
    }
    
    // Test 3: The comment is not unique - has similar text before it
    println!("\n=== Test 3: Comment has similar text nearby ===");
    {
        let mut base = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..5 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut base, "  let foo = bar;").unwrap();
        writeln!(&mut base, "  // comment to delete").unwrap();
        writeln!(&mut base, "  let baz = qux;").unwrap();
        for i in 5..10 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut ours = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..5 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut ours, "  let foo = bar;").unwrap();
        for i in 0..10 { writeln!(&mut ours, "  new_line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut ours, "  // comment to delete").unwrap();
        writeln!(&mut ours, "  let baz = qux;").unwrap();
        for i in 5..10 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut theirs = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..5 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut theirs, "  let foo = bar;").unwrap();
        // comment deleted
        writeln!(&mut theirs, "  let baz = qux;").unwrap();
        for i in 5..10 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        run_test("Test3", &base, &ours, &theirs);
    }
    
    // Test 4: Large insertion with unique marker
    println!("\n=== Test 4: Large insertion (50 lines) ===");
    {
        let mut base = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut base, "// UNIQUE_MARKER").unwrap();
        for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut ours = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        for i in 0..50 { writeln!(&mut ours, "inserted_line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut ours, "// UNIQUE_MARKER").unwrap();
        for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut theirs = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        // marker deleted
        for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        run_test("Test4", &base, &ours, &theirs);
    }
}
ENDOFFILE

    #[test]
    fn reproduce_myers_false_conflict() {
        use std::io::Write;
        
        // Test case: insert many lines before a comment, delete that comment
        // Similar to the PR description scenario
        let mut base = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut base, "// UNIQUE_COMMENT_TO_DELETE").unwrap();
        for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut ours = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        for i in 0..50 { writeln!(&mut ours, "inserted_line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut ours, "// UNIQUE_COMMENT_TO_DELETE").unwrap();
        for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut theirs = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        // comment deleted
        for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        for (algo, algo_name) in [
            (imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, "Myers"),
            (imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram, "Histogram"),
        ] {
            let mut out = Vec::new();
            let mut input = imara_diff::InternedInput::default();
            let options = builtin_driver::text::Options {
                diff_algorithm: algo,
                conflict: Conflict::Keep {
                    style: ConflictStyle::Merge,
                    marker_size: 7.try_into().unwrap(),
                },
            };
            let resolution = builtin_driver::text(
                &mut out,
                &mut input,
                Default::default(),
                &ours,
                &base,
                &theirs,
                options,
            );
            println!("{}: {:?}", algo_name, resolution);
            if resolution == Resolution::Conflict {
                println!("Output:\n{}", std::str::from_utf8(&out).unwrap());
            }
        }
    }
ENDOFFILE

    #[test]
    fn reproduce_myers_false_conflict() {
        use std::io::Write;
        
        // Test case: insert many lines before a comment, delete that comment
        // Similar to the PR description scenario
        let mut base = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut base, "// UNIQUE_COMMENT_TO_DELETE").unwrap();
        for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut ours = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        for i in 0..50 { writeln!(&mut ours, "inserted_line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut ours, "// UNIQUE_COMMENT_TO_DELETE").unwrap();
        for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut theirs = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        // comment deleted
        for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        for (algo, algo_name) in [
            (imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, "Myers"),
            (imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram, "Histogram"),
        ] {
            let mut out = Vec::new();
            let mut input = imara_diff::InternedInput::default();
            let options = builtin_driver::text::Options {
                diff_algorithm: algo,
                conflict: builtin_driver::text::Conflict::Keep {
                    style: builtin_driver::text::ConflictStyle::Merge,
                    marker_size: 7.try_into().unwrap(),
                },
            };
            let resolution = builtin_driver::text(
                &mut out,
                &mut input,
                Default::default(),
                &ours,
                &base,
                &theirs,
                options,
            );
            println!("{}: {:?}", algo_name, resolution);
            if resolution == Resolution::Conflict {
                println!("Output:\n{}", std::str::from_utf8(&out).unwrap());
            }
        }
    }
ENDOFFILE
echo "done"

+            let mut input = imara_diff::InternedInput::default();

+                diff_algorithm: algo,
+                conflict: Conflict::Keep {
+                    style: ConflictStyle::Merge,
+                    marker_size: 7.try_into().unwrap(),

+            };

+                &mut out,
+                &mut input,
+                Default::default(),

+                &base,
+                &theirs,
+                options,
+            );
+            println!("{}: {:?}", algo_name, resolution);
+            if resolution == Resolution::Conflict {
+                println!("Output:\n{}", std::str::from_utf8(&out).unwrap());
+            }
+        }
+    }

cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/repro_test.rs << 'ENDOFFILE'
use std::io::Write;

fn run_test(description: &str, base: &[u8], ours: &[u8], theirs: &[u8]) {
    let mut output = Vec::new();
    let mut input = imara_diff::InternedInput::new(&[][..], &[][..]);
    
    for algo in [imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram] {
        let options = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Options {
            diff_algorithm: algo,
            conflict: gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Conflict::Keep {
                style: gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::ConflictStyle::Merge,
                marker_size: std::num::NonZeroU8::new(7).unwrap(),
            },
        };
        let labels = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::Labels::default();
        
        output.clear();
        input.clear();
        
        let resolution = gix_merge::blob::builtin_driver::text::function::merge(
            &mut output, &mut input, labels, ours, base, theirs, options,
        );
        let algo_name = if algo == imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers { "Myers" } else { "Histogram" };
        println!("{} [{}]: {:?}", description, algo_name, resolution);
        if resolution == gix_merge::blob::Resolution::Conflict {
            println!("  Output:\n{}", String::from_utf8_lossy(&output));
            // Check for conflict markers
            let s = String::from_utf8_lossy(&output);
            if s.contains("<<<<<<<") {
                println!("  HAS CONFLICT MARKERS!");
            }
        }
    }
}

fn main() {
    // Test 1: Simple insert before unique line, delete that line
    println!("=== Test 1: Insert before unique line, delete that line ===");
    {
        let base = b"line_a\nunique_comment\nline_b\n";
        let ours = b"line_a\nnew1\nnew2\nnew3\nunique_comment\nline_b\n";
        let theirs = b"line_a\nline_b\n";
        run_test("Test1", base, ours, theirs);
    }
    
    // Test 2: More lines
    println!("\n=== Test 2: More context lines ===");
    {
        let mut base = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..10 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut base, "// unique comment").unwrap();
        for i in 10..20 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut ours = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..10 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        for i in 0..10 { writeln!(&mut ours, "new_line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut ours, "// unique comment").unwrap();
        for i in 10..20 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut theirs = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..10 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        for i in 10..20 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        run_test("Test2", &base, &ours, &theirs);
    }
    
    // Test 3: Large insertion
    println!("\n=== Test 3: Large insertion (50 lines) ===");
    {
        let mut base = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut base, "// UNIQUE_MARKER").unwrap();
        for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut ours = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        for i in 0..50 { writeln!(&mut ours, "inserted_line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut ours, "// UNIQUE_MARKER").unwrap();
        for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut theirs = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        // marker deleted
        for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
        
        run_test("Test3", &base, &ours, &theirs);
    }
    
    // Test 4: The exact scenario from the PR but small
    println!("\n=== Test 4: Non-unique context ===");
    {
        let mut base = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..5 { writeln!(&mut base, "  const x = {};", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut base, "  // comment").unwrap();
        for i in 5..10 { writeln!(&mut base, "  const y = {};", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut ours = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..5 { writeln!(&mut ours, "  const x = {};", i).unwrap(); }
        for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut ours, "  const new_{} = foo;", i).unwrap(); }
        writeln!(&mut ours, "  // comment").unwrap();
        for i in 5..10 { writeln!(&mut ours, "  const y = {};", i).unwrap(); }
        
        let mut theirs = Vec::new();
        for i in 0..5 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "  const x = {};", i).unwrap(); }
        // comment deleted
        for i in 5..10 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "  const y = {};", i).unwrap(); }
        
        run_test("Test4", &base, &ours, &theirs);
    }
}

cd /testbed && cat > /testbed/gix-merge/tests/repro_test.rs << 'ENDOFFILE'
use std::io::Write;
use gix_merge::blob::{
    builtin_driver,
    builtin_driver::text::{Conflict, ConflictStyle},
    Resolution,
};

#[test]
fn reproduce_myers_false_conflict() {
    // Test case: insert many lines before a comment, delete that comment
    let mut base = Vec::new();
    for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
    writeln!(&mut base, "// UNIQUE_COMMENT_TO_DELETE").unwrap();
    for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
    
    let mut ours = Vec::new();
    for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
    for i in 0..50 { writeln!(&mut ours, "inserted_line{}", i).unwrap(); }
    writeln!(&mut ours, "// UNIQUE_COMMENT_TO_DELETE").unwrap();
    for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
    
    let mut theirs = Vec::new();
    for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
    // comment deleted
    for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
    
    for (algo, algo_name) in [
        (imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, "Myers"),
        (imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram, "Histogram"),
    ] {
        let mut out = Vec::new();
        let mut input = imara_diff::InternedInput::default();
        let options = builtin_driver::text::Options {
            diff_algorithm: algo,
            conflict: Conflict::Keep {
                style: ConflictStyle::Merge,
                marker_size: 7.try_into().unwrap(),
            },
        };
        let resolution = builtin_driver::text(
            &mut out,
            &mut input,
            Default::default(),
            &ours,
            &base,
            &theirs,
            options,
        );
        println!("{}: {:?}", algo_name, resolution);
        if resolution == Resolution::Conflict {
            println!("Output:\n{}", String::from_utf8_lossy(&out));
        }
        
        // Assert that both algorithms produce the same (non-conflict) result
        // This is the expected behavior: the deletion should not conflict with insertion
        if algo == imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers {
            assert!(
                resolution != Resolution::Conflict,
                "Myers algorithm produced a false conflict"
            );
        }
    }
}
ENDOFFILE
echo "done"

use std::io::Write;
use gix_merge::blob::{
    builtin_driver,
    builtin_driver::text::{Conflict, ConflictStyle},
    Resolution,
};

#[test]
fn reproduce_myers_false_conflict() {
    // Test case: insert many lines before a comment, delete that comment
    let mut base = Vec::new();
    for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
    writeln!(&mut base, "// UNIQUE_COMMENT_TO_DELETE").unwrap();
    for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut base, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
    
    let mut ours = Vec::new();
    for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
    for i in 0..50 { writeln!(&mut ours, "inserted_line{}", i).unwrap(); }
    writeln!(&mut ours, "// UNIQUE_COMMENT_TO_DELETE").unwrap();
    for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut ours, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
    
    let mut theirs = Vec::new();
    for i in 0..20 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
    // comment deleted
    for i in 20..40 { writeln!(&mut theirs, "line{}", i).unwrap(); }
    
    // First, print the diffs to understand what's happening
    println!("=== Base -> Ours (Myers) ===");
    {
        let input = imara_diff::InternedInput::new(base.as_slice(), ours.as_slice());
        let diff = imara_diff::Diff::compute(imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, &input);
        for hunk in diff.hunks() {
            println!("  before: {:?}, after: {:?}", hunk.before, hunk.after);
        }
    }
    
    println!("=== Base -> Theirs (Myers) ===");
    {
        let input = imara_diff::InternedInput::new(base.as_slice(), theirs.as_slice());
        let diff = imara_diff::Diff::compute(imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, &input);
        for hunk in diff.hunks() {
            println!("  before: {:?}, after: {:?}", hunk.before, hunk.after);
        }
    }
    
    println!("=== Base -> Ours (Histogram) ===");
    {
        let input = imara_diff::InternedInput::new(base.as_slice(), ours.as_slice());
        let diff = imara_diff::Diff::compute(imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram, &input);
        for hunk in diff.hunks() {
            println!("  before: {:?}, after: {:?}", hunk.before, hunk.after);
        }
    }
    
    println!("=== Base -> Theirs (Histogram) ===");
    {
        let input = imara_diff::InternedInput::new(base.as_slice(), theirs.as_slice());
        let diff = imara_diff::Diff::compute(imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram, &input);
        for hunk in diff.hunks() {
            println!("  before: {:?}, after: {:?}", hunk.before, hunk.after);
        }
    }
    
    for (algo, algo_name) in [
        (imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, "Myers"),
        (imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram, "Histogram"),
    ] {
        let mut out = Vec::new();
        let mut input = imara_diff::InternedInput::default();
        let options = builtin_driver::text::Options {
            diff_algorithm: algo,
            conflict: Conflict::Keep {
                style: ConflictStyle::Merge,
                marker_size: 7.try_into().unwrap(),
            },
        };
        let resolution = builtin_driver::text(
            &mut out,
            &mut input,
            Default::default(),
            &ours,
            &base,
            &theirs,
            options,
        );
        println!("{} resolution: {:?}", algo_name, resolution);
        if resolution == Resolution::Conflict {
            println!("{} output:\n{}", algo_name, String::from_utf8_lossy(&out));
        }
    }
}
ENDOFFILE

The second condition `right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start` catches this.\n- If right.before is non-empty [X, Y) and left.before is empty [Y, Y): right.before.contains(&left.before.start) = [X,Y).contains(&Y) = false. In git\'s model, no. The insertion adds new lines at position 20, and the deletion removes line 20. They\'re independent changes.\n\nSo we need to also skip the first condition when one of the ranges is empty. Let me refine:\n\n```rust\nfn left_overlaps_right(left: &Hunk, right: &Hunk) -> bool {\n    if left.side == right.side {\n        return false;\n    }\n    // Both empty at same position → both insertions at same spot, this is a conflict\n    if left.before.is_empty() && right.before.is_empty() {\n        return left.before.start == right.before.start;\n    }\n    // If either is empty (pure insertion), it can\'t overlap with a non-empty hunk\n    if left.before.is_empty() || right.before.is_empty() {\n        return false;\n    }\n    // Both non-empty: check if ranges overlap\n    right.before.contains(&left.before.start)\n}\n```\n\nWait, but I need to double-check: can there be a case where we have two insertions that should conflict? They shouldn\'t conflict, and with the fix they won\'t (since `left.before.start != right.before.start`).\n\nLet me also check: what if we have a case where both sides modify the same line?
