- Base -> Ours: `before: 20..20, after: 20..70` (pure insertion of 50 lines at position 20)
- Base -> Theirs: `before: 20..21, after: 20..20` (pure deletion of 1 line at position 20)

And BOTH produce a conflict! This means the issue is not in the diff algorithm itself, but in the merge logic. Both algorithms produce the correct diff hunks, but the merge still sees a conflict.

Let me look at the `take_intersecting` function more carefully:

The hunks are:
- Current (ours): before=[20, 20), after=[20, 70), side=Current
- Other (theirs): before=[20, 21), after=[20, 20), side=Other

After sorting by `before.start`, both start at 20. Now in `take_intersecting`:

1. Take the first hunk (ours) into `input`: before=[20, 20), after=[20, 70), side=Current
2. Check if next hunk (theirs) overlaps: `left_overlaps_right(theirs, ours)`:
   - `theirs.side != ours.side` → true
   - `ours.before.contains(&theirs.before.start)` = `[20, 20).contains(&20)` → false (empty range doesn't contain anything)
   - `ours.before.is_empty() && ours.before.start == theirs.before.start` = `true && 20 == 20` → **true**!

So it considers a pure insertion (empty before range) at position X as overlapping with a deletion at position X! This is the bug.

An insertion at position X (before=empty, after=non-empty) should NOT conflict with a deletion at position X. The insertion adds new content, and the deletion removes different content. These are independent changes.

Let me verify: Git's merge-file correctly resolves this because it doesn't consider empty hunks (pure insertions) as overlapping with other hunks at the same position.

Let me look at the `left_overlaps_right` function:

```rust
fn left_overlaps_right(left: &Hunk, right: &Hunk) -> bool {
    left.side != right.side
        && (right.before.contains(&left.before.start)
            || (right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start))
}
```

The condition `right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start` is the problem. When `right` is a pure insertion (empty before), it matches ANY `left` that starts at the same position. This causes pure insertions to be treated as overlapping with any change at the same position.

But wait, the function is called with different arguments in different contexts. Let me trace through the algorithm:

In the first loop (line 434):
```rust
while iter.peek().filter(|b_hunk| left_overlaps_right(b_hunk, hunk)).is_some() {
    intersecting.extend(iter.next());
}
```
Here, `hunk` is from `input` (ours), `b_hunk` is from `iter` (next hunks). So `left = b_hunk` (theirs), `right = hunk` (ours).
- `right` (ours) has empty before range → `right.before.is_empty()` is true
- `right.before.start == left.before.start` → 20 == 20 → true
→ They overlap!

In the second loop (line 440-448):
```rust
while intersecting
    .last_mut()
    .zip(iter.peek_mut())
    .filter(|(last_intersecting, candidate)| left_overlaps_right(candidate, last_intersecting))
    .is_some()
```
Here, `candidate` is from iter (ours side), `last_intersecting` is from intersecting (theirs side). So `left = candidate` (ours), `right = last_intersecting` (theirs).
- `right` (theirs) has non-empty before range [20, 21) → `right.before.is_empty()` is false
- `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` → [20, 21).contains(&20) → true
→ They overlap!

So both checks pass. The issue is that the overlap detection is too broad. An insertion should not conflict with a deletion at the same position.

Now, the fix: the condition `right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start` should probably be removed, or modified. When `right` has an empty before range (pure insertion), it shouldn't overlap with anything. An insertion adds new content that doesn't conflict with deletions.

But wait, there's also the case where BOTH sides are pure insertions at the same position. That could be a conflict (both sides add different content at the same spot). Let me think...

Actually, in git's 3-way merge:
- If both sides insert at the same position (both have before=empty at position X), that IS a conflict if the inserted content differs.
- If one side inserts and the other side deletes at the same position, that should NOT be a conflict. The deletion removes something from the base, and the insertion adds something new. They don't conflict.

So the fix should be: an empty before range should NOT trigger overlap with a non-empty before range. Both must be empty for it to be a conflict (both insertions at same spot), or both must have overlapping non-empty ranges.

Wait, let me reconsider. The current logic in the first loop checks:
- `right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start` 

This catches the case where `right` (the hunk already in `input`) is a pure insertion. But we also need to check if `left` (the candidate) is also a pure insertion. If both are insertions at the same spot, it's a conflict. If only one is an insertion, no conflict.

But actually, the condition is asymmetric. Let me look at how the function is called in both loops:

Loop 1: `left_overlaps_right(b_hunk, hunk)` where `b_hunk` is the peeked item (from iterator), `hunk` is from `input`.
- If `hunk` (right) is a pure insertion and `b_hunk` (left) starts at the same position, they overlap.

Loop 2: `left_overlaps_right(candidate, last_intersecting)` where `candidate` is from iterator (same side as input), `last_intersecting` is from intersecting (other side).
- If `last_intersecting` is empty and `candidate` starts at the same position, they overlap.

The fix should check that BOTH hunks have empty before ranges for it to be an overlap when one is empty. Or better: if one hunk has an empty before range (pure insertion) and the other has a non-empty before range, they should NOT overlap.

Let me think about this more carefully. What are all the overlap scenarios?

1. Both have non-empty before ranges that intersect → conflict (both modified same lines)
2. Both have empty before ranges at the same position → conflict (both inserted at same spot)
3. One has empty before, one has non-empty before at the same position → NOT a conflict (one inserted, other deleted/changed different content)
4. One has empty before at position X, other has non-empty before that contains X → This is the same as case 3.

So the fix should be: for two hunks to overlap, EITHER:
- Both have non-empty before ranges that intersect, OR
- Both have empty before ranges at the same position.

Let me look at the `left_overlaps_right` function and fix it:

```rust
fn left_overlaps_right(left: &Hunk, right: &Hunk) -> bool {
    left.side != right.side
        && (right.before.contains(&left.before.start)
            || (right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start))
}
```

The problem is the second condition. It should also require `left.before.is_empty()`. But we also need to handle the case where `left.before.contains(&right.before.start)` (the reverse check). Actually, let me think about what "overlap" means:

Two hunks overlap if they affect overlapping regions of the base file. A hunk with empty before range affects no base lines (it's a pure insertion). A hunk with non-empty before range affects base lines.

So: if right has empty before, it doesn't affect any base lines → it can't overlap with anything based on before ranges. BUT if left also has empty before, they both insert at the same point, which IS a conflict.

Let me rewrite:

```rust
fn left_overlaps_right(left: &Hunk, right: &Hunk) -> bool {
    if left.side == right.side {
        return false;
    }
    // Both empty at same position → overlap (both insertions at same spot)
    if left.before.is_empty() && right.before.is_empty() && left.before.start == right.before.start {
        return true;
    }
    // If either is empty (pure insertion), no overlap with non-empty hunks
    if left.before.is_empty() || right.before.is_empty() {
        return false;
    }
    // Both non-empty: check if ranges intersect
    right.before.contains(&left.before.start) 
        || left.before.contains(&right.before.start)
}
```

Wait, but I need to be careful about the semantics. The function is called `left_overlaps_right` and the existing logic only checks one direction (`right.before.contains(&left.before.start)`). Let me check if the iteration order guarantees that this is sufficient...

The hunks are sorted by `before.start`. So `left.before.start <= right.before.start` (since left comes from the iterator which is sorted, and right is from `input` which got the first hunk). Actually, let me verify: in loop 1, `hunk` is from `input` (which was the first item from iter), and `b_hunk` is from `iter.peek()`. Since iter is sorted by `before.start`, we have `hunk.before.start <= b_hunk.before.start`. So `right.before.start <= left.before.start`.

So if `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)`, that means the right hunk's range extends at least to the start of the left hunk. Since left starts at or after right, this means the ranges overlap.

But what if left's range contains right's start? That would be `left.before.contains(&right.before.start)`. But since `right.before.start <= left.before.start`, this can only happen if they start at the same position and left extends further. In that case, `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` would also be true (if right's range is non-empty and includes that start point).

Actually, wait: if right.before = [20, 21) and left.before = [20, 22), then right.before.contains(&20) = true (20 is in [20, 21)), so the check works.

If right.before = [20, 21) and left.before = [21, 22), then right.before.contains(&21) = false. But left.before.contains(&20) = false either. So they don't overlap, which is correct.

If right.before = [20, 21) and left.before = [19, 22), but this can't happen because left starts after right (sorted). Actually wait, left is peeked from iter, and iter is sorted. So left.before.start >= right.before.start. So left can't start before right.

So the single direction check (`right.before.contains(&left.before.start)`) is actually sufficient for non-empty ranges because of the sort order!

Now let me think about the empty cases again with the sort order:
- If right.before is empty [X, X) and left.before is non-empty [X, Y): right.before.contains(&left.before.start) = [X,X).contains(&X) = false. The second condition `right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start` catches this.
- If right.before is non-empty [X, Y) and left.before is empty [Y, Y): right.before.contains(&left.before.start) = [X,Y).contains(&Y) = false. This is NOT caught by the second condition. But should it overlap?

Actually, if right.before = [20, 21) (deletion) and left.before = [21, 21) (insertion at position 21), these don't overlap. The deletion removes line 20, and the insertion adds something after it. That's fine.

But if right.before = [20, 21) (deletion) and left.before = [20, 20) (insertion at position 20), then `right.before.contains(&20)` = true (20 is in [20, 21)). The first condition catches this. And this IS currently treated as an overlap. But is it correct?

If we delete line 20 and also insert new content at line 20, are these conflicting? Git's merge-file would say no - the deletion removes the old content, and the insertion adds new content. They don't conflict.

Actually, let me reconsider with git's behavior. In the PR description:
- Ours: inserts ~70 lines before a comment (comment moves from line 32 to line 102)
- Theirs: deletes the comment at line 32

Git merge-file resolves this cleanly. The insertion and deletion don't conflict.

But the current code sees:
- Ours: before=[20, 20), after=[20, 70) — insertion at position 20
- Theirs: before=[20, 21), after=[20, 20) — deletion of line 20

The overlap check:
- Loop 1: `left_overlaps_right(theirs, ours)`:
  - `ours.before.contains(&theirs.before.start)` = `[20,20).contains(&20)` = false
  - `ours.before.is_empty() && ours.before.start == theirs.before.start` = true && 20 == 20 = **true** → overlap!

So the bug is that a pure insertion on one side is treated as overlapping with a deletion on the other side at the same position.

The fix should ensure that a pure insertion only overlaps with another pure insertion at the same position, not with a deletion/modification.

Let me now implement the fix:

```rust
fn left_overlaps_right(left: &Hunk, right: &Hunk) -> bool {
    left.side != right.side
        && (right.before.contains(&left.before.start)
            || (right.before.is_empty() && left.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start))
}
```

This changes the second condition to require BOTH before ranges to be empty. When only one is empty, it falls through to the first condition which will be false (since an empty range doesn't contain anything). 

But wait, there's also the case in loop 2 where `left_overlaps_right(candidate, last_intersecting)`:
- `candidate` is from iter (same side as input), `last_intersecting` is from intersecting (other side)
- If `last_intersecting` (right) has non-empty before and `candidate` (left) has empty before at a position inside right's range:
  - `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` — if left is at same position as right.start, this is true!
  
For example: right.before = [20, 21), left.before = [20, 20). Then right.before.contains(&20) = true. So this would still be treated as overlap.

But is this correct? A deletion at [20, 21) and an insertion at [20, 20) — should these conflict? In git's model, no. The insertion adds new lines at position 20, and the deletion removes line 20. They're independent changes.

So we need to also skip the first condition when one of the ranges is empty. Let me refine:

```rust
fn left_overlaps_right(left: &Hunk, right: &Hunk) -> bool {
    if left.side == right.side {
        return false;
    }
    // Both empty at same position → both insertions at same spot, this is a conflict
    if left.before.is_empty() && right.before.is_empty() {
        return left.before.start == right.before.start;
    }
    // If either is empty (pure insertion), it can't overlap with a non-empty hunk
    if left.before.is_empty() || right.before.is_empty() {
        return false;
    }
    // Both non-empty: check if ranges overlap
    right.before.contains(&left.before.start)
}
```

Wait, but I need to double-check: can there be a case where we have two insertions that should conflict? Yes, if both sides insert different content at the same position. That should be a conflict.

But what about two insertions at different positions? They shouldn't conflict, and with the fix they won't (since `left.before.start != right.before.start`).

Let me also check: what if we have a case where both sides modify the same line? For example:
- Ours: before=[20, 21), after=[20, 21) — changed line 20
- Theirs: before=[20, 21), after=[20, 21) — also changed line 20

These are both non-empty and `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` = [20,21).contains(&20) = true → overlap. Correct!

What if ours changes lines 20-25 and theirs changes lines 22-28?
- Ours: before=[20, 26)
- Theirs: before=[22, 29)
- `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` = [20,26).contains(&22) = true → overlap. Correct!

Now, let me also think about the second loop in `take_intersecting`:

```rust
while intersecting
    .last_mut()
    .zip(iter.peek_mut())
    .filter(|(last_intersecting, candidate)| left_overlaps_right(candidate, last_intersecting))
    .is_some()
{
    input.extend(iter.next());
    found_more_intersections = true;
}
```

This extends `input` with more hunks from the same side that overlap with the intersecting hunks. For example:
- Input has ours hunk: before=[20, 21), after=[20, 21)
- Intersecting has theirs hunk: before=[20, 22), after=[20, 22)

But the theirs hunk extends to line 22, and there might be another ours hunk at [21, 23) that also overlaps. This second loop catches that.

With my fix, pure insertions won't be caught in the first loop, so they won't end up in `intersecting`, and the second loop won't matter for them.

Base -> Theirs (Myers):

In `function.rs`, lines 161-183:
```rust
Conflict::ResolveWithOurs | Conflict::ResolveWithTheirs => {
    let (our_hunks, their_hunks) = match filled_hunks_side {
        Side::Current => (&current_hunks, &intersecting),
        Side::Other => (&intersecting, &current_hunks),
        Side::Ancestor => {
            unreachable!("initial hunks are never ancestors")
        }
    };
    if hunks_differ_in_diff3(ConflictStyle::Diff3, our_hunks, their_hunks, input, &current_tokens) {
        resolution = Resolution::CompleteWithAutoResolvedConflict;
    }
    let hunks_to_write = if conflict == Conflict::ResolveWithOurs {
        our_hunks
    } else {
        their_hunks
    };
    if let Some(first_hunk) = hunks_to_write.first() {
        write_ancestor(input, ancestor_integrated_until, first_hunk.before.start as usize, out);
    }
    write_hunks(hunks_to_write, input, &current_tokens, out);
    if let Some(last_hunk) = hunks_to_write.last() {
        ancestor_integrated_until = last_hunk.before.end;
    }
}
```

So for `ResolveWithTheirs`, it writes the `their_hunks`. But then `ancestor_integrated_until` is set to `last_hunk.before.end`, which should skip the ancestor part that was covered by these hunks.

cd /testbed && cat > /testbed/gix-merge/tests/repro_test2.rs << 'ENDOFFILE'
use std::io::Write;
use gix_merge::blob::{
    builtin_driver,
    builtin_driver::text::{Conflict, ConflictStyle},
    Resolution,
};

#[test]
fn debug_zdiff3_interesting_merge_theirs() {
    // Recreate zdiff3-interesting test case
    let base = b"1\n2\n3\n4\n5\n6\n7\n8\n9\n";
    let ours = b"1\n2\n3\n4\nA\nB\nC\nD\nE\nF\nG\nH\nI\nJ\n7\n8\n9\n";
    let theirs = b"1\n2\n3\n4\nA\nB\nC\n5\n6\nG\nH\nI\nJ\n7\n8\n9\n";
    
    // First show diffs
    println!("=== Base -> Ours ===");
    {
        let input = imara_diff::InternedInput::new(base.as_slice(), ours.as_slice());
        let diff = imara_diff::Diff::compute(imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, &input);
        for hunk in diff.hunks() {
            println!("  before: {:?}, after: {:?}", hunk.before, hunk.after);
        }
    }
    
    println!("=== Base -> Theirs ===");
    {
        let input = imara_diff::InternedInput::new(base.as_slice(), theirs.as_slice());
        let diff = imara_diff::Diff::compute(imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, &input);
        for hunk in diff.hunks() {
            println!("  before: {:?}, after: {:?}", hunk.before, hunk.after);
        }
    }
    
    for (algo, algo_name) in [
        (imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, "Myers"),
        (imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram, "Histogram"),
    ] {
        let mut out = Vec::new();
        let mut input = imara_diff::InternedInput::default();
        let options = builtin_driver::text::Options {
            diff_algorithm: algo,
            conflict: Conflict::ResolveWithTheirs,
        };
        let resolution = builtin_driver::text(
            &mut out,
            &mut input,
            Default::default(),
            &ours,
            &base,
            &theirs,
            options,
        );
        println!("{} (merge-theirs): {:?}", algo_name, resolution);
        println!("Output:\n{}", String::from_utf8_lossy(&out));
        println!("Expected:\n{}", String::from_utf8_lossy(theirs));
    }
}
ENDOFFILE
echo "done"

use gix_merge::blob::{
    builtin_driver,
    builtin_driver::text::Conflict,
};

#[test]
fn debug_zdiff3_interesting_merge_theirs() {
    // Recreate zdiff3-interesting test case
    let base: &[u8] = b"1\n2\n3\n4\n5\n6\n7\n8\n9\n";
    let ours: &[u8] = b"1\n2\n3\n4\nA\nB\nC\nD\nE\nF\nG\nH\nI\nJ\n7\n8\n9\n";
    let theirs: &[u8] = b"1\n2\n3\n4\nA\nB\nC\n5\n6\nG\nH\nI\nJ\n7\n8\n9\n";
    
    // First show diffs
    println!("=== Base -> Ours ===");
    {
        let input = imara_diff::InternedInput::new(base, ours);
        let diff = imara_diff::Diff::compute(imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, &input);
        for hunk in diff.hunks() {
            println!("  before: {:?}, after: {:?}", hunk.before, hunk.after);
        }
    }
    
    println!("=== Base -> Theirs ===");
    {
        let input = imara_diff::InternedInput::new(base, theirs);
        let diff = imara_diff::Diff::compute(imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, &input);
        for hunk in diff.hunks() {
            println!("  before: {:?}, after: {:?}", hunk.before, hunk.after);
        }
    }
    
    for (algo, algo_name) in [
        (imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, "Myers"),
        (imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram, "Histogram"),
    ] {
        let mut out = Vec::new();
        let mut input = imara_diff::InternedInput::default();
        let options = builtin_driver::text::Options {
            diff_algorithm: algo,
            conflict: Conflict::ResolveWithTheirs,
        };
        let resolution = builtin_driver::text(
            &mut out,
            &mut input,
            Default::default(),
            ours,
            base,
            theirs,
            options,
        );
        println!("{} (merge-theirs): {:?}", algo_name, resolution);
        println!("Output:\n{}", String::from_utf8_lossy(&out));
        println!("Expected:\n{}", String::from_utf8_lossy(theirs));
    }
}
ENDOFFILE

No, that\'s not right either.\n\nActually, let me think about this more carefully. In git\'s 3-way merge:\n\n1. If side A modifies lines L1..L2, and side B also modifies any lines in L1..L2 (including insertions at any point in that range), it\'s a conflict.\n2. If side A inserts at position P, and side B deletes at position P, it\'s NOT a conflict.\n3. If side A inserts at position P, and side B also inserts at position P, it IS a conflict (if the insertions differ).\n\nSo the rule is:\n- Insertion vs Deletion at same point: no conflict\n- Insertion vs Insertion at same point: conflict\n- Modification vs Modification in overlapping ranges: conflict\n- Insertion inside a Modification range: conflict\n- Modification that contains an Insertion point: conflict\n\nThe current overlap check `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` handles case 5: if right\'s before range contains left\'s start point, they overlap. But for empty ranges (insertions), `contains` is always false.\n\nThe second condition `right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start` was meant to handle case 3: both insertions at the same point.\n\nBut it also incorrectly catches case 2: insertion vs deletion at the same point.\n\nAnd it does NOT catch case 4: insertion inside a modification range (because it only checks if right is empty, not left).\n\nWait, actually case 4 IS caught by the first condition! So `!left.after.is_empty()` means left is NOT a pure deletion. If left is a modification (both non-empty) or an insertion (before empty, after non-empty), then this is a true overlap.\n\nBut what about the case where left is also an insertion? `left.after` would be non-empty. So `!left.after.is_empty()` would be true. ✓\n\nWhat about the case where left is a modification? `left.after` would be non-empty. ✓\n\nWhat about the case where left is a deletion? `left.after` would be empty. So `!left.after.is_empty()` = false. ✗ (no false overlap) ✓\n\nBut wait, there\'s a subtlety: what if left is a deletion at position X, and right is an insertion at position X? Now I can see the issue clearly. Look at the diffs:

- `before: 6..6, after: 9..13` (insert 4 lines at position 6: G H I J)

So theirs has TWO hunks: one pure insertion at position 4 (before the changed region), and one pure insertion at position 6 (after the changed region). Note that theirs kept lines 5 and 6 unchanged (they're in the base and in theirs: `5\n6\n`).

The base->ours hunk has before=[4, 6) which is non-empty. 

Now with my fix:
- Ours: before=[4, 6), non-empty
- Theirs hunk 1: before=[4, 4), empty → does NOT overlap (one empty, one non-empty)
- Theirs hunk 2: before=[6, 6), empty → does NOT overlap (one empty, one non-empty)

So none of the theirs hunks overlap with the ours hunk! This means the merge treats them as independent changes. The ours hunk replaces base lines [4, 6) with A-J. The theirs hunk 1 inserts A B C at position 4, and theirs hunk 2 inserts G H I J at position 6.

But these ARE actually conflicting! In git's merge, the ours change (replace 5,6 with A-J) and theirs change (insert A B C before 5, and G H I J after 6) DO conflict because they both modify the same region.

The reason git flags this as a conflict is that the ours hunk (which spans [4,6) in base) overlaps with the region where theirs makes changes (around lines 4-6). The fact that theirs expresses its changes as insertions at the boundaries doesn't change the semantic overlap.

So my fix is too aggressive. Let me reconsider.

The problem from the PR is specifically:
- Ours: pure insertion (before=empty) at position X
- Theirs: deletion (before=non-empty) at position X

These should NOT conflict.

But what about:
- Ours: non-empty before range
- Theirs: empty before range at a position INSIDE ours's before range

These SHOULD conflict. Example:
- Ours: before=[4, 6), after=[4, 14) — replace lines 5,6 with 10 lines
- Theirs: before=[4, 4), after=[4, 7] — insert at position 4 (which is inside [4,6))

In this case, git would see a conflict: ours changed lines 5,6 and theirs inserted new content in the middle of that region.

So the key distinction is:
- If a hunk has an empty before range (pure insertion), it does NOT overlap with a non-empty before range ONLY IF the empty before range is at the exact start or end boundary of the non-empty range? No, that's not right either.

Actually, let me think about this more carefully. In git's 3-way merge:

1. If side A modifies lines L1..L2, and side B also modifies any lines in L1..L2 (including insertions at any point in that range), it's a conflict.
2. If side A inserts at position P, and side B deletes at position P, it's NOT a conflict.
3. If side A inserts at position P, and side B also inserts at position P, it IS a conflict (if the insertions differ).

So the rule is:
- Insertion vs Deletion at same point: no conflict
- Insertion vs Insertion at same point: conflict
- Modification vs Modification in overlapping ranges: conflict
- Insertion inside a Modification range: conflict
- Modification that contains an Insertion point: conflict

The current overlap check `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` handles case 5: if right's before range contains left's start point, they overlap. But for empty ranges (insertions), `contains` is always false.

The second condition `right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start` was meant to handle case 3: both insertions at the same point.

But it also incorrectly catches case 2: insertion vs deletion at the same point.

And it does NOT catch case 4: insertion inside a modification range (because it only checks if right is empty, not left).

Wait, actually case 4 IS caught by the first condition! If left is an insertion at position P, and right is a modification spanning [L1, L2) where L1 <= P < L2, then `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` = true. So the first condition handles case 4.

But what about the reverse? If left is a modification and right is an insertion at a point inside left's range? Let's see: the function is called with `(b_hunk, hunk)` in the first loop, where `hunk` is from `input` (sorted first) and `b_hunk` is from `iter` (comes after). Since sorted by `before.start`:
- If right (hunk) is modification [4, 6) and left (b_hunk) is insertion at [4, 4):
  - `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` = [4,6).contains(&4) = true → overlap. ✓
- If right (hunk) is insertion at [4, 4) and left (b_hunk) is modification [4, 6):
  - `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` = [4,4).contains(&4) = false
  - `right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start` = true && 4 == 4 = true → overlap

But in this second case, should they overlap? Right is an insertion at position 4, left is a modification of [4, 6). The insertion is at the start of the modification range. According to git, this is a conflict.

So the issue is: case 2 (insertion vs deletion at same point) is also caught by the second condition, but it shouldn't be.

The fix should distinguish between:
- insertion vs insertion at same point → conflict (keep)
- insertion vs deletion at same point → no conflict (need to fix)
- insertion vs modification at same point → conflict (keep, but this is already handled by the first condition when the modification is the right argument)

Wait, actually looking at it again: the second condition ONLY applies when `right.before.is_empty()`. If right is an insertion and left is a deletion at the same point, it triggers. If right is an insertion and left is also an insertion at the same point, it triggers (correct). If right is an insertion and left is a modification at the same point, it triggers (also correct, because we're inserting at the start of a modified region).

So the only false positive is: right is an insertion, left is a deletion at the same point. To fix this, we need to also check that `left.before` is empty (both are insertions) OR that left is a modification (non-empty before range).

Actually, let me reconsider. The condition should be: "right is an insertion, and left is NOT a pure deletion at the same point". More precisely:

- If right is empty and left is empty → conflict (both insertions)
- If right is empty and left is non-empty → conflict (insertion inside modification range)
- If right is empty and left is non-empty but left's after is empty → NOT a conflict (insertion vs deletion at same point)

Wait, that's getting complicated. Let me think about what the "after" range tells us. A hunk with:
- before=empty, after=non-empty → pure insertion
- before=non-empty, after=empty → pure deletion
- before=non-empty, after=non-empty → modification

So the false positive is: right is insertion (before empty, after non-empty), left is deletion (before non-empty, after empty) at the same point.

Actually, the simplest fix: the second condition should require that `left.before` is also non-empty OR `left.after` is non-empty (i.e., left is not a pure deletion). 

But actually, even simpler: the original condition was:
```rust
right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start
```

This catches all cases where right is an insertion at the same point as left. The only false positive is when left is a deletion at that same point. So we just need to exclude that case:

```rust
right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start && !left.after.is_empty()
```

Wait, but `left.after.is_empty()` means left is a pure deletion. So `!left.after.is_empty()` means left is NOT a pure deletion. If left is a modification (both non-empty) or an insertion (before empty, after non-empty), then this is a true overlap.

But what about the case where left is also an insertion? `left.after` would be non-empty. So `!left.after.is_empty()` would be true. ✓

What about the case where left is a modification? `left.after` would be non-empty. ✓

What about the case where left is a deletion? `left.after` would be empty. So `!left.after.is_empty()` = false. ✗ (no false overlap) ✓

But wait, there's a subtlety: what if left is a deletion at position X, and right is an insertion at position X? In the first loop, `left = b_hunk` (theirs), `right = hunk` (ours). If ours inserts at X and theirs deletes at X, this checks `right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start && !left.after.is_empty()`. Since left is a deletion, `left.after` is empty, so this is false. Good.

But what about the second loop? `left_overlaps_right(candidate, last_intersecting)`:
- `candidate` is from iter (same side as input), `last_intersecting` is from intersecting (other side)
- If input had an insertion, and intersecting has a deletion at the same point, then:
  - `right = last_intersecting` = deletion (non-empty before, empty after)
  - `left = candidate` = insertion (empty before, non-empty after)
  - First condition: `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` = [X, X+1).contains(&X) = true → overlap!

Wait, that's a problem. In the second loop, if intersecting has a deletion at position X, and candidate is an insertion at position X, the first condition catches it as an overlap.

Hmm, but should they overlap? Let me think:
- Input (ours): pure insertion at position X
- Intersecting (theirs): pure deletion at position X

We're in the second loop, which means input already has an insertion, intersecting already has a deletion (they were matched in the first loop because of the second condition). Now the second loop is checking if there are more hunks from the input side that also overlap with the intersecting side.

But wait, if my fix to the first condition prevents the initial overlap, we wouldn't even get to the second loop! Because the first loop wouldn't put the deletion into intersecting.

- `current_hunks` = [theirs deletion]
- `intersecting` = [ours insertion]

But wait, this is the same scenario! The order of hunks determines which side is "input" and which is "intersecting". If the deletion comes first (sorted by before.start), it goes to input, and the insertion goes to intersecting. Then they're treated as conflicting.

So my fix to the first condition only works when the insertion comes before the deletion in sorted order. When the deletion comes first, we still get a false conflict because `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` catches the insertion's start point inside the deletion's range.

Hmm, so I need to also fix the first condition. Let me think...

The first condition `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` should also exclude the case where left is a pure insertion (empty before) and right is a pure deletion (non-empty before, empty after). But that's hard because we only have the before ranges to work with.

Actually, let me think about what git does. In git's merge, an insertion at the same point as a deletion does NOT conflict. The insertion adds new content, the deletion removes old content. They're independent.

So the general rule should be: if one side has a pure insertion (empty before) and the other side has a pure deletion (empty after), they don't conflict regardless of position.

But the condition `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` doesn't check after ranges. 

Let me add a pre-condition to `left_overlaps_right`: if one hunk is a pure insertion (empty before) and the other is a pure deletion (empty after), they don't overlap.

```rust
fn left_overlaps_right(left: &Hunk, right: &Hunk) -> bool {
    if left.side == right.side {
        return false;
    }
    // A pure insertion on one side and a pure deletion on the other never conflict
    if (left.before.is_empty() && right.after.is_empty()) 
        || (right.before.is_empty() && left.after.is_empty()) {
        return false;
    }
    // Both empty at same position → both insertions, this is a conflict
    if left.before.is_empty() && right.before.is_empty() {
        return left.before.start == right.before.start;
    }
    // Both non-empty or one empty + one modification: check range overlap
    right.before.contains(&left.before.start)
        || (right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start)
}
```

Wait, but the original condition `right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start` also catches the case where right is an insertion and left is a modification. That's correct (insertion inside modification range). 

But with my new pre-condition, if right is insertion (empty before) and left is deletion (empty after), we return false. And if right is insertion and left is modification (non-empty after), we fall through to the second condition which returns true. 

And if right is deletion (non-empty before, empty after) and left is insertion (empty before), the pre-condition catches it and returns false. 

And if right is modification (non-empty before, non-empty after) and left is insertion (empty before), the pre-condition doesn't apply, and `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` catches it. Wait, does it? If right.before = [4, 6) and left.before = [4, 4), then `[4,6).contains(&4)` = true. Yes!

If right is insertion (empty before) and left is modification (non-empty before), the pre-condition doesn't apply (left.after is non-empty), and we fall to the second condition: `right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start` = true (if at same position). This correctly identifies the overlap.

Let me also consider: what if right is insertion and left is insertion but at DIFFERENT positions? The second condition checks `right.before.start == left.before.start`, so they won't match. Correct.

What about the second loop? `left_overlaps_right(candidate, last_intersecting)`:
- If `last_intersecting` is deletion and `candidate` is insertion at the same point: pre-condition catches it → false. 
- If `last_intersecting` is insertion and `candidate` is deletion at the same point: pre-condition catches it → false. 

Now, there's one more edge case: what if both sides have empty before AND empty after? That would be a hunk that neither adds nor removes anything. This shouldn't happen in practice (diff algorithms don't produce such hunks). So we don't need to worry about it.

Let me implement this more complete fix:

   439	            return left.before.start == right.before.start;
   440	        }
   441	        // Both non-empty or one empty + one modification: check range overlap
   442	        right.before.contains(&left.before.start)
   443	            || (right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start)
   444	    }
   445	
   446	    loop {
   447	        let hunk = input.last().expect("just pushed");
Review the changes and make sure they are as expected. Edit the file again if necessary.

Now let me think about edge cases more carefully:

1. **Both sides insert at the same position**: Should conflict. Let me verify:
   - Left: before=[X, X), after=[X, Y) 
   - Right: before=[X, X), after=[X, Z)
   - My code: pre-condition doesn't apply (both have non-empty after). Both empty check: `left.before.is_empty() && right.before.is_empty()` = true, `left.before.start == right.before.start` = true → overlap. ✓

2. **One side inserts, other side modifies at same position**:
   - Left: before=[X, X+1), after=[X, X+2) (modification)
   - Right: before=[X, X), after=[X, Y) (insertion)
   - My code: pre-condition doesn't apply (right has non-empty after). Both empty check: right is empty but left is not → skip. Third part: `right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start` = true → overlap. ✓

3. **One side deletes, other side inserts at same position**: 
   - Left: before=[X, X+1), after=[X, X) (deletion)
   - Right: before=[X, X), after=[X, Y) (insertion)
   - My code: pre-condition `right.before.is_empty() && left.after.is_empty()` = true && true → return false. No overlap. ✓

4. **One side modifies, other side deletes at same position**:
   - Left: before=[X, X+1), after=[X, X+2) (modification)
   - Right: before=[X, X+1), after=[X, X) (deletion)
   - My code: pre-condition doesn't apply (left has non-empty after). Both non-empty: `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` = [X, X+1).contains(&X) = true → overlap. ✓

5. **Both sides delete at same position**:
   - Left: before=[X, X+1), after=[X, X) (deletion)
   - Right: before=[X, X+1), after=[X, X) (deletion)
   - My code: pre-condition doesn't apply. Both non-empty: `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` = true → overlap. ✓
   - (But actually both sides deleting the same thing is not a conflict in practice, but it's handled as one and then resolved trivially since the content is the same.)

6. **Insertion vs insertion at different positions**: 
   - Left: before=[X, X), after=[X, Y)
   - Right: before=[Z, Z), after=[Z, W)
   - My code: pre-condition doesn't apply. Both empty: `left.before.start == right.before.start` = X == Z = false → no overlap. ✓

7. **Insertion at position inside a modification range**:
   - Left: before=[X, Y), after=[X, Z) (modification)
   - Right: before=[P, P), after=[P, Q) where X < P < Y (insertion inside range)
   - But wait, right is sorted after left? Since sorted by before.start, and X < P, left comes first. So:
     - In first loop: `left_overlaps_right(b_hunk=right, hunk=left)`:
       - `left = right` (insertion), `right = left` (modification)
       - `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` = [X, Y).contains(&P) = true → overlap. ✓

8. **Deletion inside a modification range**:
   - Left: before=[X, Y), after=[X, Z) (modification)
   - Right: before=[P, P+1), after=[P, P) (deletion inside range)
   - `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` = [X, Y).contains(&P) = true → overlap. ✓

9. **Modification that ends where an insertion begins**:
   - Left: before=[X, Y), after=[X, Z) (modification)
   - Right: before=[Y, Y), after=[Y, W) (insertion at end of modification)
   - `right.before.contains(&left.before.start)` = [X, Y).contains(&X) = true (left starts at X which is in [X, Y)) → overlap. ✓

10. **Insertion at start of a deletion**:
    - Left: before=[X, Y), after=[X, X) (deletion)
    - Right: before=[X, X), after=[X, Z) (insertion)
    - Pre-condition: `right.before.is_empty() && left.after.is_empty()` = true && true → return false. No overlap. This is the exact case we want to fix! ✓

   417	pub fn take_intersecting(
   418	    iter: &mut Peekable<impl Iterator<Item = Hunk>>,
   419	    input: &mut Vec<Hunk>,
   420	    intersecting: &mut Vec<Hunk>,
   421	) -> Option<()> {
   422	    input.clear();
   423	    input.push(iter.next()?);
   424	    intersecting.clear();
   425	
   426	    fn left_overlaps_right(left: &Hunk, right: &Hunk) -> bool {
   427	        if left.side == right.side {
   428	            return false;
   429	        }
   430	        // A pure insertion on one side and a pure deletion on the other side never conflict.
   431	        // They affect different parts of the file: one adds new content, the other removes old content.
   432	        if (left.before.is_empty() && right.after.is_empty())
   433	            || (right.before.is_empty() && left.after.is_empty())
   434	        {
   435	            return false;
   436	        }
   437	        // Both empty at same position → both insertions at same spot, this is a conflict
   438	        if left.before.is_empty() && right.before.is_empty() {
   439	            return left.before.start == right.before.start;
   440	        }
   441	        // Both non-empty or one empty + one modification: check range overlap
   442	        right.before.contains(&left.before.start)
   443	            || (right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start)
   444	    }
   445	
   446	    loop {
   447	        let hunk = input.last().expect("just pushed");
   448	        while iter.peek().filter(|b_hunk| left_overlaps_right(b_hunk, hunk)).is_some() {
   449	            intersecting.extend(iter.next());
   450	        }
   451	        // The hunks that overlap might themselves overlap with a following hunk of the other side.
   452	        // If so, split it so it doesn't overlap anymore.
   453	        let mut found_more_intersections = false;
   454	        while intersecting
   455	            .last_mut()
   456	            .zip(iter.peek_mut())
   457	            .filter(|(last_intersecting, candidate)| left_overlaps_right(candidate, last_intersecting))
   458	            .is_some()
   459	        {
   460	            input.extend(iter.next());

use gix_merge::blob::{
    builtin_driver,
    builtin_driver::text::{Conflict, ConflictStyle},
};

#[test]
fn check_spurious_c_conflicts() {
    let base = b"int f(int x, int y)\n{\n  if (x == 0)\n  {\n    return y;\n  }\n  return x;\n}\n\nint g(size_t u)\n{\n  while (u < 30)\n  {\n    u++;\n  }\n  return u;\n}\n";
    let ours = b"int g(size_t u)\n{\n  while (u < 30)\n  {\n    u++;\n  }\n  return u;\n}\n\nint h(int x, int y, int z)\n{\n  if (z == 0)\n  {\n    return x;\n  }\n  return y;\n}\n";
    let theirs = b"int f(int x, int y)\n{\n  if (x == 0)\n  {\n    return y;\n  }\n  return x;\n}\n\nint g(size_t u)\n{\n  while (u > 34)\n  {\n    u--;\n  }\n  return u;\n}\n";
    
    for (algo, algo_name) in [
        (imara_diff::Algorithm::Myers, "Myers"),
        (imara_diff::Algorithm::Histogram, "Histogram"),
    ] {
        let mut out = Vec::new();
        let mut input = imara_diff::InternedInput::default();
        let options = builtin_driver::text::Options {
            diff_algorithm: algo,
            conflict: Conflict::Keep {
                style: ConflictStyle::Merge,
                marker_size: 7.try_into().unwrap(),
            },
        };
        let resolution = builtin_driver::text(
            &mut out,
            &mut input,
            Default::default(),
            ours,
            base,
            theirs,
            options,
        );
        println!("{}: {:?}", algo_name, resolution);
        println!("Output:\n{}", String::from_utf8_lossy(&out));
    }
}
ENDOFFILE

+        if left.side == right.side {
+            return false;
+        }
+        // A pure insertion on one side and a pure deletion on the other side never conflict.
+        // They affect different parts of the file: one adds new content, the other removes old content.
+        if (left.before.is_empty() && right.after.is_empty())
+            || (right.before.is_empty() && left.after.is_empty())
+        {
+            return false;
+        }
+        // Both empty at same position → both insertions at same spot, this is a conflict
+        if left.before.is_empty() && right.before.is_empty() {
+            return left.before.start == right.before.start;
+        }
+        // Both non-empty or one empty + one modification: check range overlap
+        right.before.contains(&left.before.start)
+            || (right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start)
     }

All 22 tests pass.

Let me now submit:</think>All 22 tests pass. The fix addresses the issue where a pure insertion on one side and a pure deletion on the other side at the same position were incorrectly treated as overlapping/conflicting in the 3-way merge.

The change is in the `left_overlaps_right` function in `/testbed/gix-merge/src/blob/builtin_driver/text/utils.rs`. The key insight is:

1. **Pure insertion** (empty `before` range, non-empty `after` range) + **Pure deletion** (non-empty `before` range, empty `after` range) at the same position: These should NOT conflict because they affect different parts of the file - one adds new content, the other removes old content.

2. **Pure insertion** + **Pure insertion** at the same position: These SHOULD conflict (both sides add different content at the same spot).

3. **Non-empty** + **Non-empty** overlapping ranges: These SHOULD conflict (both sides modify the same lines).

The fix adds an early return for case 1, checking if one side has an empty `before` (pure insertion) and the other has an empty `after` (pure deletion). It also properly handles case 2 by checking if both `before` ranges are empty at the same position.



🎬 ACTION
submit

+            return false;

+        // A pure insertion on one side and a pure deletion on the other side never conflict.
+        // They affect different parts of the file: one adds new content, the other removes old content.
+        if (left.before.is_empty() && right.after.is_empty())
+            || (right.before.is_empty() && left.after.is_empty())
+        {
+            return false;
+        }
+        // Both empty at same position → both insertions at same spot, this is a conflict
+        if left.before.is_empty() && right.before.is_empty() {
+            return left.before.start == right.before.start;
+        }
+        // Both non-empty or one empty + one modification: check range overlap
+        right.before.contains(&left.before.start)
+            || (right.before.is_empty() && right.before.start == left.before.start)
     }
